# Program Progress Matrix

This document is the durable human-readable rollup for progress toward a WordPress distribution whose first-party runtime logic is authored in Haxe and whose generated artifacts remain functional for the WordPress ecosystem.

Beads remains the task database. This matrix is a status ledger over Beads issues, receipts, manifests, and PRD milestones. Update it in the same change whenever milestone status, scope, evidence gates, Gutenberg split policy, or completion estimates change.

Last updated: 2026-07-09
Source checkpoint: `WPHX-403`
Tracking issue: `WPHX-000.02`

Date note: this matrix is updated on the local project date. Some existing checkpoint paragraphs preserve receipt-recorded UTC dates from prior evidence artifacts rather than being rewritten during later planning updates.

## Super Progress

Current super progress toward "WordPress completely in Haxe and functional": **46.4%**.

This is an evidence-weighted program estimate, not source-line completion. It gives credit for proven target foundations, ABI/linker infrastructure, vertical WordPress slices, and executable parity gates, but it discounts shell/scaffold work and gives almost no credit for Gutenberg/browser ownership until `WPHX-400` and `WPHX-500` start producing package-level receipts.

| Area | Weight | Current | Contribution | Basis |
| --- | ---: | ---: | ---: | --- |
| Program governance, baselines, manifests, Beads, receipts | 10 | 95 | 9.5 | `WPHX-000`, `WPHX-800`, baseline receipts, locked sibling repo policy |
| PHP target feasibility, ABI, linker, public boundary foundation | 20 | 100 | 20.0 | `WPHX-100` and `WPHX-200` closed |
| WordPress PHP runtime Haxe ownership | 40 | 38.4 | 15.4 | `WPHX-300` has verified vertical slices, first-party PHP manifest ownership/split closure, bounded domain closures through WPHX-306/WPHX-307/WPHX-308/WPHX-309/WPHX-310/WPHX-312/WPHX-313/WPHX-314/WPHX-315/WPHX-316/WPHX-318/WPHX-319/WPHX-320, extensive WPHX PHP public-adapter and WP_Http helper/request candidate evidence. WPHX-314 is bounded closed across block/interactivity inventory, typed adapter-contract, copied-oracle fixtures, selected upstream PHPUnit ratchets, package-topology bridge-router block rendering observations, a helper-level typed Haxe block wrapper support candidate, and public PHP shell-gap classification showing zero durable generated WPHX-314 public shells. WPHX-315 is bounded closed across admin common/list-table inventory, typed adapter-contract, copied-oracle admin fixtures, selected upstream PHPUnit/e2e ratchet scope, package-topology bridge-router observations, a bounded typed HXX-style admin markup pilot, and bridge-router durable-claim guardrails. WPHX-316 is bounded closed across admin feature/AJAX inventory, typed adapter-contract evidence, copied-oracle route fixtures for admin AJAX/post, settings/options, taxonomy, privacy export/erase, and plugin management, selected upstream PHPUnit ratchets, and selected installed/browser e2e gate declarations. WPHX-318 is bounded closed across XML-RPC/legacy/deprecated surface inventory, typed adapter-contract evidence, copied-oracle endpoint/server fixture evidence, selected upstream XML-RPC/deprecated PHPUnit ratchets, and selected installed XML-RPC route gate declarations. WPHX-319 is bounded closed across updates/installers/upgrader/recovery surface inventory, typed adapter-contract evidence, copied-oracle updater/recovery fixture observations, selected upstream PHPUnit ratchets, and selected installed/browser update/recovery gate declarations. WPHX-320 is bounded closed across default theme PHP surface inventory, a bounded typed HXX-style theme markup pilot, selected default-theme-related upstream PHPUnit dependency ratchets, blocked browser/performance/visual ratchet declarations, selected copied-oracle default-theme pattern output fixtures, selected copied-oracle default-theme functions.php hook/callback observations, selected installed/browser default-theme rendering gate declarations, and a parent closure receipt, but no generated existing-theme-file replacement or installed theme rendering parity yet. Much of Core remains unported, and selected ratchets, blocked installed/e2e gate declarations, deterministic bridge routers, copied-oracle fixtures, representative typed markup units, surface inventories, shell-gap audits, or adapter-contract candidates do not imply broad Haxe ownership or installed parity. |
| Installed WordPress distribution behavior and ecosystem gates | 15 | 10.0 | 1.5 | `WPHX-700` has strong early gates, focused WPHX-306 auth, WPHX-307 posts/query, WPHX-308 taxonomy/comment, WPHX-309 routing/template, WPHX-310 theme, WPHX-312 HTTP/cron/mail/feed/embed plus controlled cron/mail transport, WPHX-313 media/upload, WPHX-314 block rendering, WPHX-315 admin common/list-table package-topology bridge-router gates, WPHX-316 selected upstream admin feature/AJAX ratchets, WPHX-316 selected installed/browser admin e2e gate declarations, bounded WPHX-316 closure receipts, WPHX-318 selected upstream XML-RPC/deprecated ratchets, WPHX-318 selected installed XML-RPC HTTP route gate declarations, WPHX-319 selected upstream updates/recovery ratchets, WPHX-319 selected installed/browser update/recovery gate declarations, and WPHX-320 selected default-theme-related upstream ratchets plus blocked browser/performance/visual and installed-rendering default-theme declarations, plus a provisioned selected upstream PHPUnit ratchet with 44 groups / 88 vanilla-candidate runs where WPHX-312/WPHX-313/WPHX-315/WPHX-316/WPHX-318/WPHX-319, WPHX-320 dependency, and three WPHX-314 groups classify pass/pass, while three remaining WPHX-314 baseline failures classify vanilla fail / candidate fail rather than candidate regressions. WPHX-701 through WPHX-714 are now seeded as the authoritative upstream-test, ABI/artifact, installed-trace, ecosystem, visual/a11y, security, performance, distribution, update, and release-dossier gates; they remain open, and complete installed-system parity is not closed. |
| Browser, classic JS, Gutenberg package ownership | 10 | 0 | 0.0 | `WPHX-401` establishes the genes-ts 1.13.0 both-output-mode CI gate, and `WPHX-403` advances the pin to `b7012fa42bac67dbc08546b5acd29aec6181bdfc` after generic `genes-798` compiler fixes pass full CI. `WPHX-402` classifies 245 locked Gutenberg workspace manifests, 13,615 JS/JSX/TS/TSX modules, 3,405 preliminary static package API symbols, and 869 shipped JavaScript artifacts with zero unclassified records. `WPHX-403` proves one real zero-dependency `@wordpress/escape-html` TS→Haxe→strict generated-TS runtime roundtrip. These are compiler-platform, inventory, and bounded feasibility evidence—not reviewed Haxe package ownership; WPHX-404 through WPHX-409, WPHX-500/WPHX-501 through WPHX-512, and WPHX-600/WPHX-601 through WPHX-609 remain open. |
| Security, performance, reliability, and release closure | 5 | 0 | 0.0 | early security corpus exists and WPHX-710 through WPHX-714 are now explicit authoritative gates, but full nonfunctional and release closure remains future work |

The score should move only when evidence moves. A closed task can increase confidence in a slice without implying that the whole source area is ported.

2026-07-09 WPHX-403 checkpoint: `manifests/genes-ts/wphx-403-f8-escape-html.v1.json` and `receipts/genes-ts/wphx-403-f8-escape-html.v1.json` select the real zero-dependency forward-Gutenberg `@wordpress/escape-html` 3.48.0 leaf package at commit `98a796c8780c480ef7bcfe03c42302d9564d785c`. The gate materializes the two locked upstream TypeScript runtime modules, runs a strict TypeScript oracle, converts them with experimental ts2hx, compiles the generated Haxe twice through genes-ts with deterministic output, strict-typechecks the generated TypeScript with zero `any`/`unknown` user-module findings, and executes differential assertions across all seven package exports. The first attempt reduced module-private declaration, `RegExp.test`, and regex `String.replace` gaps into generic sibling issue `genes-798`; the landed fix at `b7012fa42bac67dbc08546b5acd29aec6181bdfc` passes the compiler repository's full CI before the root pin advances. The super-progress score stays unchanged because generated Haxe is migration evidence rather than reviewed idiomatic Haxe package ownership, WPHX-404/F9 React/TSX remains open, and no package exports, WordPress script handles, bundles, installed browser behavior, or distribution artifacts are yet owned by Haxe.

2026-07-09 WPHX-402 checkpoint: `manifests/genes-ts/wphx-402-browser-inventory.v1.json` and `receipts/genes-ts/wphx-402-browser-inventory.v1.json` derive the browser work surface from the locked WPHX-006 source/artifact JSONL authorities plus the dashboard package/API indexes and package manifests read directly from the embedded Gutenberg commit `a2a354cf35e5b69c3330d6c1cfd42d8dc2efb9fd` and forward Gutenberg commit `98a796c8780c480ef7bcfe03c42302d9564d785c`. The inventory records 245 workspace manifests across 122 embedded and 123 forward packages, with 232 manifest `exports` contracts, four legacy entry-field contracts, and nine packages with no runtime entry; it classifies 13,615 browser source modules across 8,263 JavaScript, 93 JSX, 2,304 TSX, and 2,955 TypeScript units; it links 3,405 preliminary static package API symbols; and it classifies all 869 shipped JavaScript artifacts across the WordPress 7.0 distribution and embedded Gutenberg build. Closure is zero for unclassified workspaces, modules, artifacts, unknown module packages, and static API entries without packages. Static export extraction remains inventory evidence rather than a complete API-compatibility claim. The super-progress score stays unchanged because this adds no Haxe-authored package ownership, generated browser artifact parity, runtime behavior, script-handle parity, F8/F9 feasibility, installed browser behavior, or release closure.

The WordPressHX gate reruns complete CI under locked Node 20.19.3 and records classic Genes split-ESM JavaScript runtime assertions plus genes-ts standard/minimal/full/TSX TypeScript output, strict typechecks, snapshots, source maps, todoapp API/Playwright smoke, OSV/secret/version checks, and ts2hx snapshots/roundtrips. The two pre-existing untracked genes report archives remain outside the pin. The super-progress score stays unchanged because this proves the browser compiler platform only; package ownership, classic-script ownership, installed browser behavior, and release parity remain open.

ADR-004 clarifies ownership claims without changing the score: PHP is the privileged compatibility host for current parity, Haxe owns both migrated semantics and adapter intent, and Rust/native/WASM/custom-target providers are future optional providers only for narrowly eligible kernels or explicitly named profiles with PHP fallbacks and native-on/native-off evidence. The 2026-06-29 original-path PHP emission oracle response further clarifies the current compiler split: stock Haxe PHP is the private implementation emitter; WPHX PHP is the staged custom compiler lane currently focused on bounded WordPress original-path public adapters; the portable long-term asset is Haxe-owned semantics plus typed adapter contracts, not generated PHP text. ADR-013 now makes that adapter contract explicit: WPHX PHP lowers typed Haxe source and metadata into Adapter IR file/declaration plans before printing original-path public PHP, and those annotations/IR nodes should be shaped as future inputs to a broader WPHX PHP backend or extracted `reflaxe.php` target without Haxe source rewrites. ADR-015 clarifies the Reflaxe nuance and generated-code quality bar: WPHX PHP uses Reflaxe infrastructure, but it is not yet a mature arbitrary-Haxe `reflaxe.php` target, and promotion to full backend scope requires backend-scale evidence, quality gates, and a later ADR or amendment. ADR-016 changes the focus: WPHX PHP compiler usability is now the near-term priority for new WordPress public PHP emission and compiler-shape gaps, with stock Haxe PHP bounded to private-output/stdphp oracle duty until the `WPHX-COMP-PHP-USABLE` gates move responsibility. ADR-017 keeps stock Haxe PHP as the runtime/std behavior oracle and borrowing source for boot, arrays, maps, iterators, closures, exceptions, strings, JSON, and debug/source-map behavior until a later backend-promotion ADR moves that ownership. The 2026-07-03 pivot-soundness oracle response keeps the WPHX PHP pivot sound with amber conditions: stay in-repo on staged Adapter IR / reusable PHP core IR / WordPress-profile scope, start extraction hygiene but not an extracted `reflaxe.php` target, keep stock Haxe PHP in its private-emitter/stdphp oracle role, and add profile-accretion, continuous adoption, private-emitter, plugin/reflection/stack-trace, and whole-file inventory gates before stronger backend or full-file claims. A later multi-target track, including a browser/WASM profile potentially based on `back2dos/wasmix`, a Go profile potentially based on `fullofcaffeine/reflaxe.go`, and a Rust profile potentially based on `fullofcaffeine/reflaxe.rust`, is tracked as a long-term research option and does not contribute to current parity progress. Future ownership rollups should distinguish semantic ownership, adapter-contract ownership, emission strategy, execution provider, and evidence level.

The project will focus on making WPHX PHP usable as the primary WordPress PHP compiler path before accumulating more broad Core port debt. The new gates are stock-target/gap inventory, runtime/std strategy, reusable PHP core lowering, a small whole-file WordPress pilot, and adoption CI. The super-progress score stays unchanged because this is strategy and task-shape movement, not new compiler functionality, runtime ownership, or installed WordPress behavior.

## Gutenberg Plan

The plan remains: **WordPress PHP first, browser platform feasibility next, Gutenberg package port in a sibling repo only when justified.**

1. Keep `../gutenberg` as the forward Gutenberg 23.4 oracle checkout. Do not mix it into the WordPress 7.0 distribution track without an ADR.
2. Use this repo for `WPHX-400` feasibility: genes-ts output mode, package exports, WordPress script handles, React/TSX or HHX policy, source maps, bundling, globals, and browser tests.
3. Create `../gutenberghx` only after the first real package and React/TSX feasibility gates pass, currently described as after `WPHX-403` and `WPHX-404`, or earlier only by ADR.
4. When `gutenberghx` exists, keep this repo as the program authority: root Beads database, PRD, release claims, lock manifests, distribution integration, and final receipts.
5. Let `gutenberghx` own Haxe source for Gutenberg packages, package-level fixtures, generated package artifacts, and package parity receipts.
6. Port packages by dependency layer. Start with small leaf packages and package-shape fixtures, then move toward shared primitives and editor/block packages only after exports, React semantics, data stores, source maps, and build output are proven.
7. Smaller libraries stay in this repo unless they need independent release cadence, reusable compiler-pressure fixtures, or sustained parallel ownership. If split later, they still need lock manifests and receipts consumed by this repo.

## Update Rules

Update this file when any of the following changes:

- a `WPHX-*` parent milestone opens, closes, is seeded, or has meaningful child progress;
- a task changes the super-progress estimate or its weights;
- a receipt creates new evidence for Haxe ownership, parity, ABI, generated-code shape, distribution behavior, or nonfunctional closure;
- the Gutenberg/gutenberghx trigger, baseline, or cross-repo workflow changes;
- a shell/scaffold graduates to verified Haxe-owned logic, or a verified slice is downgraded because evidence was found weak;
- an ADR changes the PRD milestone shape, baseline policy, compiler strategy, or test authority.

Progress claims in chat or handoff notes should point back here, Beads, and receipts. Do not let this matrix become a second task database.
